                10.1021/acsnano.1c02023</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D15%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D11607-11618%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DJ.%2BPeng%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BChen%26author%3DG.%2BLiang%26author%3DS.%2BHu%26author%3DT.%2BZhou%26author%3DF.%2BZheng%26author%3DQ.%2BPan%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DQ.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26title%3DPhase%2BCompatible%2BNiFe2O4%2BCoating%2BTunes%2BOxygen%2BRedox%2Bin%2BLi-Rich%2BLayered%2BOxide%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.1c02023&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c17554&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.1c02023&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phase Compatible NiFe2O4 Coating Tunes Oxygen Redox in Li-Rich Layered Oxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Jiming; Li, Yu; Chen, Zhiqiang; Liang, Gemeng; Hu, Sijiang; Zhou, Tengfei; Zheng, Fenghua; Pan, Qichang; Wang, Hongqiang; Li, Qingyu; Liu, Jianwen; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11607-11618</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-rich layered oxides have attracted intense attention for lithium-ion batteries, as provide substantial capacity from transition metal cation redox simultaneous with reversible oxygen-anion redox.  However, unregulated irreversible oxygen-anion redox leads to crit. issues such as voltage fade and oxygen release.  Here, we report a feasible NiFe2O4 (NFO) surface-coating strategy to turn the nonbonding coordination of surface oxygen into metal-oxygen decoordination.  In particular, the surface simplex M-O (M = Ni, Co, Mn from MO6 octahedra) and N-O (N = Ni, Fe from NO6 octahedra) bonds are reconstructed in the form of M-O-N bonds.  By applying both in operando and ex situ technologies, we found this heterostructural interface traps surface lattice oxygen, as well as restrains cation migration in Li-rich layered oxide during electrochem. cycling.  Therefore, surface lattice oxygen behavior is significantly sustained.  More interestingly, we directly observe the surface oxygen redox decouple with cation migration.  In addn., the NFO-coating blocks HF produced from electrolyte decompn., resulting in reducing the dissoln. of Mn.  With this strategy, higher cycle stability (91.8% at 1 C after 200 cycles) and higher rate capability (109.4 mA g-1 at 1 C) were achieved in this work, compared with pristine Li-rich layered oxide.  Our work offers potential for designing electrode materials utilizing oxygen redox chem.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpEDW4_1UaUpLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhKtj7LDJ5GUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtlOhsrzL&amp;md5=60d7f0e1d8752c2168c65885e3dbe44d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref5'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1039/c6cs00776g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-Ion Batteries: Present and Future</span>. <i>Chem. Soc. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>46</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3529</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3614</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c6cs00776g</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D46%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D3529-3614%26journal%3DChem.%2BSoc.%2BRev.%26author%3DJ.-Y.%2BHwang%26author%3DS.-T.%2BMyung%26author%3DY.-K.%2BSun%26title%3DSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%253A%2BPresent%2Band%2BFuture%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc6cs00776g&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c17554&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc6cs00776g&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhKtj7LDJ5GUQ"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1021/acsnano.1c01518</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D15%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D8896-8906%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DH.%2BHe%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DD.%2BHuang%26author%3DJ.%2BLuan%26author%3DS.%2BLiu%26author%3DW.%2BK.%2BPang%26author%3DD.%2BSun%26author%3DY.%2BTang%26author%3DW.%2BZhou%26author%3DL.%2BHe%26author%3DC.%2BZhang%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26title%3DElectron-Injection-Engineering%2BInduced%2BPhase%2BTransition%2Btoward%2BStabilized%2B1T-MoS2%2Bwith%2BExtraordinary%2BSodium%2BStorage%2BPerformance%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.1c01518&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c17554&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.1c01518&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electron-Injection-Engineering Induced Phase Transition toward Stabilized 1T-MoS2 with Extraordinary Sodium Storage Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Hanna; Li, Xiaolong; Huang, Dan; Luan, Jinyi; Liu, Sailin; Pang, Wei Kong; Sun, Dan; Tang, Yougen; Zhou, Wenzheng; He, Lirong; Zhang, Chuhong; Wang, Haiyan; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8896-8906</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Phase transition engineering, with the ability to alter the electronic structure and physicochem. properties of materials, has been widely used to achieve the thermodynamically unstable metallic phase MoS2 (1T-MoS2), although the complex operating conditions and low yield of previous strategies make the large-scale fabrication of 1T-MoS2 a big challenge.  Herein, we report a facile electron injection strategy for phase transition engineering and fabricate a composite of conductive TiO chem. bonded to 1T-MoS2 nanoflowers (TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs) on a large scale.  The underlying mechanism anal. reveals that electron-injection-engineering triggers a reorganization of the Mo 4d orbitals and results in a 100% phase transition of MoS2 from 2H to 1T.  In the TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs composite, the 1T-MoS2 demonstrates a higher electronic cond., a lower Na+ diffusion barrier, and a more restricted S release than 2H-MoS2.  In addn., conductive TiO bonding successfully resolves the stability challenge of the 1T phase.  These merits endow TiO-1T-MoS2 NFs electrodes with an excellent rate capability (650/288 mAh g-1 at 50/20 000 mA g-1, resp.) and an outstanding cyclability (501 mAh g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 after 700 cycles) in sodium ion batteries.  Such an improvement signifies that this facile and scalable phase-transition engineering combined with a deep mechanism anal. offers an important ref. for designing advanced materials for various applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpyKYJHdQ-rObVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liOMsXio354Cg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtVCiu73M&amp;md5=558f10b755b08b37912246dde8ae2aef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.1c06576"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xing, X.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Cation-Disordered O3-Na<sub>0.8</sub>Ni<sub>0.6</sub>Sb<sub>0.4</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Cathode for High-Voltage Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS App Mater.                 10.1021/acsami.1c06576</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D32948-32956%26journal%3DACS%2BApp%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DL.%2BYu%26author%3DX.-X.%2BXing%26author%3DS.-Y.%2BZhang%26author%3DX.%2BZhang%26author%3DX.%2BHan%26author%3DP.-F.%2BWang%26author%3DS.%2BXu%26title%3DCation-Disordered%2BO3-Na0.8Ni0.6Sb0.4O2%2BCathode%2Bfor%2BHigh-Voltage%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.1c06576&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c17554&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.1c06576&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sb-C nanofibers are synthesized successfully through a single-nozzle electrospinning technique and subsequent calcination.  The structural and morphol. characterizations reveal the uniform nanofiber structure with the Sb nanoparticles embedded homogeneously in the carbon nanofibers.  Electrochem. expts. show that the Sb-C nanofiber electrode can deliver large reversible capacity (631 mA h g-1) at C/15, greatly improved rate capability (337 mA h g-1 at 5 C) and excellent cycling stability (90% capacity retention after 400 cycles).                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High capacity group-15 alloy anodes for Na-ion batteries: Electrochemical and mechanical insights</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mortazavi, Majid; Ye, Qiongjie; Birbilis, Nick; Medhekar, Nikhil V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Group-15 elements P, As, Sb and Bi offer the prospect of serving as functional alloying elements for developing high-capacity alloy anodes for Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Here the authors obtain concn.-dependent electrochem. properties of Na alloys with group-15 elements using 1st principles calcns.  Since Na intercalation in these alloys is accompanied by a substantial vol. expansion that can lead to mech. failure and loss of capacity, the authors have also obtained a full set of concn.-dependent elastic properties for a single crystal as well as a polycryst. microstructure.  Sodiation of these alloys results in their significant elastic softening by as large as 60%.  In contrast to the group-14 alloys that are also being explored as anodes of NIBs, the elastic softening in group-15 alloys varies in a nonmonotonic manner with Na concn., and more importantly, the max. degrdn. of elastic properties does not necessarily occur at full sodiation.  The authors' results provide crucial insights into the electrochem. and mech. response of these alloys to Na intercalation, thus contributing to the design of failure-resistant architectures of high capacity NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSJQsodyMFLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhc1LpIBW7rOw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVantrc%253D&amp;md5=e9f64d13e5651087f3170658a6061757</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2010.07.020"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.-J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Review of the Electrochemical Performance of Alloy Anodes for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A review of the electrochemical performance of alloy anodes for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Wei-Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">196</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Alloy anodes are promising anode materials for lithium-ion batteries due to their high-energy capacity and safety characteristics.  However, the com. use of alloy anodes has been hindered to date by their low cycle life and high initial capacity loss.  This overview highlights the recent progress in improving and understanding the electrochem. performance of various alloy anodes.  The approaches used for performance improvement are summarized, and the causes of first-cycle irreversible capacity loss are discussed.  The capacity retentions and irreversible capacity losses of various alloy anodes are compared.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insights on the Mechanism of Na-Ion Storage in Soft Carbon Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jian, Zelang; Bommier, Clement; Luo, Langli; Li, Zhifei; Wang, Wentao; Wang, Chongmin; Greaney, P. Alex; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">29</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2314-2320</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0897-4756</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite is the com. anode for lithium-ion batteries; however, it fails to extend its success to sodium-ion batteries.  Recently, we demonstrated that a low-cost amorphous carbon-soft carbon exhibits remarkable rate performance and stable cycling life of Na-ion storage.  However, its Na-ion storage mechanism has remained elusive, which has plagued further development of such carbon anodes.  Here, we remedy this shortfall by presenting the results from an integrated set of exptl. and computational studies that, for the first time, reveal the storage mechanism for soft carbon.  We find that sodium ions intercalate into graphenic layers, leading to an irreversible quasi-plateau at ∼0.5 V vs. Na+/Na as well as an irreversible expansion seen by in situ transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and X-ray diffraction (XRD).  Such a high-potential plateau is correlated to the defective local structure inside the turbostratic stacking of soft carbon and the assocd. high-binding energies with Na ions, suggesting a trapping mechanism.  On the other hand, soft carbon exhibits long sloping regions above and below the quasi-plateau during the first sodiation, where the sloping regions present highly reversible behavior.  It is attributed to the more defects contained by soft carbon revealed by neutron total scattering and the assocd. pair distribution function studies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqc4F7hAOxhR7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6WXWfGTO9gg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anisotropic, low-tortuosity and ultra-thick red P@C-Wood electrodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Longfei; Wang, Junling; Mu, Xiaowei; Liao, Can; Cai, Wei; Zhao, Zhixin; Kan, Yongchun; Xing, Weiyi; Hu, Yuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Red phosphorus (P) is considered to be the most suitable electrode for sodium-ion batteries due to its low cost, earth abundance and high theor. capacity.  Numerous studies have focused on improving the low cond. and the extremely large vol. change of red P during the cycling process.  However, these strategies heavily decrease the P mass loading in the electrode.  Herein, inspired by natural wood, we successfully develop an ultra-thick bulk red Phosphorus@Carbon-Wood (red P@C-Wood) electrode via the vaporization-condensation process.  The sodium-ion batteries assembled with the fabricated red P@C-Wood electrode provide a high areal capacity of 18 mA h cm-2 (~ 5 times those of other reported electrodes) and the P mass loading of up to 8.4 mg cm-2 (=2 times those of other reported electrodes).  The combination of red phosphorus and carbonized wood provides a new strategy for people to improve the areal energy d. of lithium and sodium batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGokhS_InT323LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6WXWfGTO9gg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">New Mechanistic Insights on Na-Ion Storage in Nongraphitizable Carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bommier, Clement; Surta, Todd Wesley; Dolgos, Michelle; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nongraphitizable carbon, also known as hard carbon, is considered one of the most promising anodes for the emerging Na-ion batteries.  The current mechanistic understanding of Na-ion storage in hard carbon is based on the "card-house" model first raised in the early 2000s.  This model describes that Na-ion insertion occurs first through intercalation between graphene sheets in turbostratic nanodomains, followed by Na filling of the pores in the carbon structure.  We tried to test this model by tuning the sizes of turbostratic nanodomains but revealed a correlation between the structural defects and Na-ion storage.  Based on our exptl. data, we propose an alternative perspective for sodiation of hard carbon that consists of Na-ion storage at defect sites, by intercalation and last via pore-filling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqegbEbsDPzrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljvP9zgmjRSqw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A zero-strain layered metal oxide as the negative electrode for long-life sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang Yuesheng; Yu Xiqian; Xu Shuyin; Bai Jianming; Xiao Ruijuan; Hu Yong-Sheng; Li Hong; Yang Xiao-Qing; Chen Liquan; Huang Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Room-temperature sodium-ion batteries have shown great promise in large-scale energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the abundant sodium resources and low cost.  Although many interesting positive electrode materials with acceptable performance have been proposed, suitable negative electrode materials have not been identified and their development is quite challenging.  Here we introduce a layered material, P2-Na0.66[Li0.22Ti0.78]O2, as the negative electrode, which exhibits only ~0.77% volume change during sodium insertion/extraction.  The zero-strain characteristics ensure a potentially long cycle life.  The electrode material also exhibits an average storage voltage of 0.75 V, a practical usable capacity of ca. 100 mAh g(-1), and an apparent Na(+) diffusion coefficient of 1 × 10(-10) cm(-2) s(-1) as well as the best cyclability for a negative electrode material in a half-cell reported to date.  This contribution demonstrates that P2-Na0.66[Li0.22Ti0.78]O2 is a promising negative electrode material for the development of rechargeable long-life sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcTF-vbNmqlKD2Gmni0r9GoKfW6udTcc2eZoFSzp5KSVarntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3sbis12gsg%253D%253D&amp;md5=34e8f318873aa7ed3226082d3df04b0f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201404549"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Ultrastable Anode for Long-Life Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Ultrastable Anode for Long-Life Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Haijun; Ren, Yang; Xiao, Dongdong; Guo, Shaohua; Zhu, Yanbei; Qian, Yumin; Gu, Lin; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are important alternative energy storage devices that have recently come again into focus for the development of large-scale energy storage devices because sodium is an abundant and low-cost material.  However, the development of electrode materials with long-term stability has remained a great challenge.  A novel anode material, a P2-type layered oxide with the chem. compn. Na2/3Co1/3Ti2/3O2, exhibits outstanding cycle stability (∼84.84% capacity retention after 3000 cycles, very small decrease in the vol.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Low-dielectric-constant polyimide aerogel composite films with low water uptake</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Jinyoung; Kwon, Jinuk; Kim, Myeongsoo; Do, Jeonguk; Lee, Daero; Han, Haksoo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Polymer Journal (Tokyo, Japan)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A polyimide aerogel (PIA) was used to synthesize low-dielec.-const. polyimide composite films.  Unlike silica aerogel (SIA) composites, the PIA films were synthesized using polyimide.  The resulting films maintained the original thermal and chem. properties of polyimide, which contribute to their homogeneity.  The dielec. const. of the aerogel composite film was decreased to ∼2.4, a value similar to that of a SIA composite film.  The increase in dielec. const. as a result of water adsorption exhibited by SIA films was counteracted by the hydrophobicity of the polyimide in the PIA film.  The PIA composite film exhibited a 3% water uptake, compared with a 29% water uptake in the SIA film, indicating that the polyimide film is the preferred choice in wet conditions.  The presence of a uniformly dispersed aerogel, a 1% thermal decompn. temp. of 589 °C and a glass transition temp. of 298 °C for the PIA composite film were confirmed by field emission SEM, thermogravimetric anal. (TGA) and differential scanning calorimetric (DSC) anal., resp.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An O3-type oxide with low sodium content as the phase-transition-free anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Chenglong; Avdeev, Maxim; Chen, Liquan; Hu, Yong-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal oxides NaxMO2 (M=transition metal) with P2 or O3 structure have attracted attention in sodium-ion batteries (NIBs).  A universal law is found to distinguish structural competition between P2 and O3 types based on the ratio of interlayer distances of the alkali metal layer d(O-Na-O) and transition-metal layer d(O-M-O).  The ratio of about 1.62 can be used as an indicator.  O3-type Na0.66Mg0.34Ti0.66O2 oxide is prepd. as a stable anode for NIBs, in which the low Na-content (ca. 0.66) usually undergoes a P2-type structure with respect to NaxMO2. In situ X-ray diffraction reveals a single-phase reaction in the discharge-charge process, which is different from the common phase transitions reported in O3-type electrodes, ensuring long-term cycling stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVLstceXrSBLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgzTXIqSz4N5A"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Cycling Stability of O3-Type Na[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 Cathode through Sn Addition for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ryu, Hoon-Hee; Han, Geumjae; Yu, Tae-Yeon; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">125</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6593-6600</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Despite their high discharge capacity, O3-type layered cathodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) suffer from rapid capacity fading caused by detrimental phase transitions.  A series of O3-type layered Na[Ni0.5Mn0.5]O2 (NM) cathodes with different amts. of Sn were synthesized in this study by using uniformly Sn-coated precursors prepd. by a wet method to address this problem.  The introduction of Sn proportionally modified the morphologies of the Sn-NM cathodes to have higher tap densities.  The cycling stability of the NM cathode with 1 mol % Sn was improved, maintaining 84.9% of its initial capacity after 100 cycles and ∼15% higher than that of the bare NM cathode.  The improvement in cycling stability is attributed to the introduced Sn, which mitigates structural distortions caused by monoclinic phase transitions and suppresses abrupt contraction during the detrimental P3'-to-O3' phase transition in the highly charged state.  In addn., the pptd. Sn nanoparticles on the cathode surface protect the internal primary particles from parasitic attacks by the infiltrated electrolyte.  The proposed strategy provides an effective method to improve the cycling stability of O3-type layered cathodes for SIBs by modifying their morphol. and inhibiting deleterious electrolyte attacks.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoP04wzbvU5V7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljaL745XyEsmw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Li-substituted hydrostable layered oxide cathode material with oriented stacking nanoplate structure for high-performance sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Shi; Xiao, Yao; Zhu, Yan-Fang; Li, Yong-Chun; Chen, Ting; Wang, Dong; Liu, Yi-Hua; Liu, Hao; Li, Yuan; Li, Chao; Wang, Gong-Ke; Liu, Yu-Xia; Song, Yang; Wu, Zhen-Guo; Zhong, Ben-He; Guo, Xiao-Dong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">412</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">128719</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As one of the most prospective transitional metal oxide cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), P2-type Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 layered oxide generally suffers from sluggish Na+ kinetics and complicated structural evolution.  Here, a stable cobalt-free manganese nickel sodium oxide (P2-Na2/3Li1/9Ni2/9Mn2/3O2) cathode material with multilayer oriented stacking nanoplates is reported, which exhibits high hydrostability realized by partial lithium element substitution for nickel.  A prominent rate capability (71.7% capacity retention at 5 C compared to 0.2 C), excellent cycling stability (78.7% capacity retention at 2 C after 300 cycles), and a promoted performance even at a higher cutoff potential of 4.4 V were displayed owing to the bifunctional strategy of chem. substitution coupled with structure modulation.  And the as-synthesized material retains its original structure and electrochem. performance after being aged in water.  Moreover, dominant Na+ capacitive storage mechanism, high thermostability, and complete solid-soln. reaction is explicitly elucidated through quant. calcn. of electrochem. kinetics and in-situ X-ray diffraction technique.  These findings reveal the importance of rational chem. substitution and structure modulation strategy, and inspire the novel design of high-performance cathode materials for rechargeable SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoI5vJ8di47erVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljaL745XyEsmw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXks1Grsrg%253D&amp;md5=d79287f1f9c3f94c59ae8500f3a53429</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202007236"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">P3/O3 Integrated Layered Oxide as High-Power and Long-Life Cathode toward Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Si-Yuan; Guo, Yu-Jie; Zhou, Ya-Nan; Zhang, Xu-Dong; Niu, Yu-Bin; Wang, En-Hui; Huang, Lin-Bo; An, Peng-Fei; Zhang, Jing; Yang, Xin-An; Yin, Ya-Xia; Xu, Sailong; Guo, Yu-Guo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">17</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2007236</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Low-cost and stable sodium-layered oxides (such as P2- and O3-phases) are suggested as highly promising cathode materials for Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Biphasic hybridization, mainly involving P2/O3 and P2/P3 biphases, is typically used to boost their electrochem. performances.  Herein, a P3/O3 intergrown layered oxide (Na2/3Ni1/3Mn1/3Ti1/3O2) as high-rate and long-life cathode for NIBs via tuning the amts. of Ti substitution in Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3-xTixO2 (x = 0, 1/6, 1/3, 2/3) is demonstrated.  The X-ray diffraction (XRD) Rietveld refinement and aberration-cor. scanning transmission electron microscopy show the co-existence of P3 and O3 phases, and d. functional theory calcn. corroborates the appearance of the anomalous O3 phase at the Ti substitution amt. of 1/3.  The P3/O3 biphasic cathode delivers an unexpected rate capability (≈88.7% of the initial capacity at a high rate of 5 C) and cycling stability (≈68.7% capacity retention after 2000 cycles at 1 C), superior to those of the sing phases P3-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2, P3-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn1/2Ti1/6O2, and O3-Na2/3Ni1/3Ti2/3O2.  The highly reversible structural evolution of the P3/O3 integrated cathode obsd. by ex situ XRD, ex situ X-ray absorption spectra, and the rapid Na+ diffusion kinetics, underpin the enhancement.  These results show the important role of P3/O3 biphasic hybridization in designing and engineering layered oxide cathodes for NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrT3qth0NlKw7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljaL745XyEsmw"> &gt;&gt; Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1186</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1194</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.201300139</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D1186-1194%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DH.%2BPan%26author%3DX.%2BLu%26author%3DX.%2BYu%26author%3DY.-S.%2BHu%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DX.-Q.%2BYang%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26title%3DSodium%2BStorage%2Band%2BTransport%2BProperties%2Bin%2BLayered%2BNa2Ti3O7for%2BRoom-Temperature%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.201300139&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c17554&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.201300139&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Storage and Transport Properties in Layered Na2Ti3O7 for Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Huilin; Lu, Xia; Yu, Xiqian; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Yang, Xiao-Qing; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1186-1194</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered sodium titanium oxide, Na2Ti3O7, is synthesized by a solid-state reaction method as a potential anode for sodium-ion batteries.  Through optimization of the electrolyte and binder, the microsized Na2Ti3O7 electrode delivers a reversible capacity of 188 mA h g-1 in 1 M NaFSI/PC electrolyte at a current rate of 0.1C in a voltage range of 0.0-3.0 V, with sodium alginate as binder.  The av. Na storage voltage plateau is found at ca. 0.3 V vs. Na+/Na, in good agreement with a first-principles prediction of 0.35 V. The Na storage properties in Na2Ti3O7 are investigated from thermodn. and kinetic aspects.  By reducing particle size, the nanosized Na2Ti3O7 exhibits much higher capacity, but still with unsatisfied cyclic properties.  The solid-state interphase layer on Na2Ti3O7 electrode is analyzed.  A zero-current overpotential related to thermodn. factors is obsd. for both nano- and microsized Na2Ti3O7.  The electronic structure, Na+ ion transport and cond. are investigated by the combination of first-principles calcn. and electrochem. characterizations.  On the basis of the vacancy-hopping mechanism, a quasi-3D energy favorable trajectory is proposed for Na2Ti3O7.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facilitating Phase Evolution for a High-Energy-Efficiency, Low-Cost O3-Type NaxCu0.18Fe0.3Mn0.52O2 Sodium Ion Battery Cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Fu, Hongwei; Fan, Guozheng; Zhou, Jiang; Yu, Xinzhi; Xie, Xuesong; Wang, Jue; Lu, Bingan; Liang, Shuquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">59</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13792-13800</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The phase transition and lattice parameter evolution of O3 structure commonly occurs in O3-type sodium ion battery (SIB) cathodes, which might enlarge the voltage hysteresis and lower the energy efficiency.  Given that the cost is one of the issues discouraging the is on application of SIBs in large-scale energy storage, here the focus on Co/Ni-free NaxCu0.18Fe0.3Mn0.52O2 (x = 0.8, 0.85, 0.9) and propose a convenient strategy to reduce the voltage hysteresis.  It is found that when the Na content is 0.8, the highest energy efficiency of 95.4% after activation is achieved (2.5-4.0 V, 50 mA g-1, the 50th cycle), in addn. to a satisfactory capacity retention (∼ 0.056% decay per cycle).  The further characterizations reveal that Na0.8Cu0.18Fe0.3Mn0.52O2 owns a gentle O3-P3 phase transition process and does not undergo O3 phase lattice parameter evolution.  The key point lies in the attainability of the O3/P3 composite of the material.  This work will provide a simple strategy for the rational design of O3-type cathodes with a high energy efficiency and might offer inspiration to search for layered oxides with a higher O3/P3 crit. Na content through element adjustments.  Facile O3-P3 phase evolution in NaxCu0.18Fe0.3Mn0.52O2 is achieved by setting the Na content at 0.8, a near-crit. value for obtaining the O3/P3 composite while preventing P2 phase.  The voltage polarization of phase transition is reduced compared with that in higher Na content samples, resulting in a lower voltage hysteresis and a better energy efficiency for Na0.8Cu0.18Fe0.3Mn0.52O2.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqWnzKtatb5BrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liEFZB5EJlNDw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhslyisrrJ&amp;md5=fcbcf15bb1834be70dbdbebf944782df</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2020.126308"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Butt, F.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-voltage P2-type manganese oxide cathode induced by titanium gradient modification for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Quanqing; Butt, Faheem K.; Guo, Zefeng; Wang, Liqin; Zhu, Youqi; Xu, Xingyan; Ma, Xilan; Cao, Chuanbao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing layered high-voltage P2-type manganese oxide with working voltage above 4.5 V incorporating into Ni2+/4+ redox and high capacity based on anionic redox has become trend to develop high energy d. sodium ion batteries.  However, capacity fading and undesired rate capability caused by serious phase transition, irreversible oxygen activity and electrolyte/electrode side reactions would occur esp. under high operating voltage besides the Jahn-Teller effect.  Here, based on anionic and cationic redox, a novel titanium gradient modification coupling with the synergic Ti-enriched surface and Ti-substituted interior is proposed to achieve excellent stability and rate capability.  As a result, the high-voltage P2-Na0.66Mn0.54Ni0.13Co0.13O2 cathode induced by titanium gradient modification can deliver a large reversible discharge capacity of 133.2 mA h g-1 with 77.9% capacity retention after 100 cycles under 4.7 V cut-off voltage at 1C (200 mA g-1), and achieve a high energy d. of 456.4 Wh kg-1.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ca-substituted P3-type NaxNi1/3Mn1/3Co1/3O2 as a potential high voltage cathode active material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Matsui, Masaki; Mizukoshi, Fumikazu; Hasegawa, Hirona; Imanishi, Nobuyuki</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">485</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">229346</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. property of the layered sodium transition metal oxide is dependent upon the reversible phase transition during the sodium intercalation/deintercalation process.  Here we synthesized Ca-doped P3-type NaxNi1/3Mn1/3Co1/3O2 as a potential cathode active material for sodium-ion batteries.  The Ca-doping leads the lattice expansion along the c-axis, due to the electrostatic repulsion between Ca2+ ions and the transition metal ions.  Even though the doped Ca2+ ions occupy Na+ sites, the Ca-doped cathode shows lower overpotential during the galvanostatic charge-discharge process.  The electrochem. impedance spectroscopy proved that the charge-transfer resistance of the Ca-doped layered oxide is lower than the Ca-free one at low cell voltage.  These results indicate that the Ca-doping enhances the mobility of the Na+ ions in the layered structure.  The doped Ca2+ ions also suppress the irreversible O3-O1 phase transition upon the full deintercalation of the sodium ions from the layered structure.  The improved stability of the Ca-doped NaxNi1/3Mn1/3Co1/3O2 leads better capacity retention during the galvanostatic cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6rVTTRh8t8rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liEFZB5EJlNDw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXktF2mtA%253D%253D&amp;md5=28f2c82a0fb084197c84b0de3b5d63a4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.9b02021"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ning, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schuck, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schumacher, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding the Multiple Effects of TiO2 Coating on NaMn0.33Fe0.33Ni0.33O2 Cathode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                 10.1021/acsaem.9b02021</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D933-942%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26author%3DW.%2BKong%26author%3DQ.%2BLi%26author%3DD.%2BNing%26author%3DG.%2BSchuck%26author%3DG.%2BSchumacher%26author%3DC.%2BSu%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26title%3DUnderstanding%2Bthe%2BMultiple%2BEffects%2Bof%2BTiO2%2BCoating%2Bon%2BNaMn0.33Fe0.33Ni0.33O2%2BCathode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BNa-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsaem.9b02021&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c17554&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsaem.9b02021&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding the Multiple Effects of TiO2 Coating on NaMn0.33Fe0.33Ni0.33O2 Cathode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Yang; Kong, Weijin; Li, Qingyuan; Ning, De; Schuck, Gotz; Schumacher, Gerhard; Su, Chunjian; Liu, Xiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">933-942</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAEMCQ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2574-0962</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">O3-type NaTMO2 (TM = transition metal) as cathodes for Na-ion batteries have aroused much interest.  But the structural instability during charge-discharge cycles and the inferior rate capability restricts their application.  In this study, we report a synergetic modification method to simultaneously increase the rate capacity and cycling stability of O3-type NaMn0.33Fe0.33Ni0.33O2(MFN) cathode material by integrating TiO2 coating and Ti4+ doping.  Moreover, the synergetic mechanism has been put forward.  First, the TiO2-coating layer prevents the side reactions on the surface, which can retain the structural integrity and stability.  Second, TiO2-coating induces Ti4+ doping which enlarges Na-O and increases the interslab spacing d.  This raises the Na+ diffusion coeff. and improves the rate performance.  Third, because of the large Ti-O bond energy, the TM-O bond shrinks when Ti4+ is doped into the transition metal site.  O-O is also shortened due to the Ti doping.  TMO2 slabs are compressed, which benefits the structural stability and the cyclic property.  Fourth, Ti doping accompanying TiO2 coating decreases Mn3+/Mn4+ and mitigates the Jahn-Teller effect.  This increases the stability of the layered structure.  The understanding of the multiroles of TiO2 coating is equally instructive for the exploration of other cathode materials for Na-ion or Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrf3zHSDvfCsLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liEFZB5EJlNDw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXislyhuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=f60a96cde694f6d0e148f933afa3e808</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1039/c6ta07589d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">You, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.-G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An O3-type NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2cathode for sodium-ion batteries with improved rate performance and cycling stability</span>. <i>J.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">45</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17660-17664</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered O3-type NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 (space group: R‾3m) was synthesized by a sol-gel method, and subjected to electrochem. characterization for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  A Na//NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 cell can deliver a reversible capacity of 141 mA h g-1 in the voltage range of 2.0-4.0 V and show a good capacity retention of 90% after 100 cycles.  A highly reversible structural evolution of O3hex.-O3'mon.-P3hex.-P3'mon.-P3''hex. upon Na+ extn. and intercalation is demonstrated to be the key factor to its excellent cycling capability.  Furthermore, the apparent diffusion coeff. of Na ions in the layered O3-type NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 composite electrode can be effectively increased by using good conductive CNTs, which is demonstrated by cyclic voltammograms and the galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique.  Thus even at a high rate of 2C, the O3-NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 cathode still exhibits a high reversible capacity of 80 mA h g-1.  The impressive sodium storage properties of O3-NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 make it a promising candidate as a pos. electrode material for rechargeable SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1lD5p8gU-jrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liEFZB5EJlNDw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhslSltbfN&amp;md5=b2912076a7e54f6d8574de9f23b4f419</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104520"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sarkar, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Manohar, C. V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mitra, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Simple Approach to Minimize the First Cycle Irreversible Loss of Sodium Titanate Anode towards the Development of Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>70</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">104520</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2020.104520</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D70%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D104520%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DA.%2BSarkar%26author%3DC.%2BV.%2BManohar%26author%3DS.%2BMitra%26title%3DA%2BSimple%2BApproach%2Bto%2BMinimize%2Bthe%2BFirst%2BCycle%2BIrreversible%2BLoss%2Bof%2BSodium%2BTitanate%2BAnode%2Btowards%2Bthe%2BDevelopment%2Bof%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2020.104520&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c17554&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2020.104520&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A simple approach to minimize the first cycle irreversible loss of sodium titanate anode towards the development of sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sarkar, Ananta; Manohar, C. V.; Mitra, Sagar</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">70</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">104520</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">First cycle irreversible loss is a major problem of any kind of anode materials in sodium-ion battery systems (SIBs).  Here, we present a stable (4000 cycles), high capacity (237 mAh g-1) and high rate capable hydrogenated metal-doped sodium titanium oxide (Na2Ti3O7) anode material for SIBs and that suffers from high 1st cycle irreversible loss (53.86%) initially.  Later, we adopted a simple chem. shorting approach where, sodium metal was kept immediate tight contact with anode material in presence of electrolyte medium to reduce the irreversible loss.  It was found that 60 min chem. shorting is enough to minimize the irreversible loss to 4.11% from 53.6% and enhance the Coulombic efficiency to 84% from 36.22% resp. without compromising the specific capacity and cycling stability.  This approach is adopted in full-cell (sodium vanadium phosphate vs. hydrogenated metal-doped Na2Ti3O7) formation and the study also provided similar improved electrochem. performance.  The current understanding and the approach provide a new direction to overcome the 1st cycle irreversible loss of sodium titanate anode and can be utilized further to develop sustainable rechargeable sodium-ion battery.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo0qOOUjIEAe7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh47t0mqhO7iA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXitVGrurk%253D&amp;md5=f5830b4cb250a9223d06be1a35ae861a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201501655"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sharma, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gonzalo, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pramudita, J. C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, M. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Brand, H. E. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hart, J. N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, W. K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rojo, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Unique Structural Evolution of the O3-Phase Na<sub>2/3</sub>Fe<sub>2/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> during High Rate Charge/Discharge: A Sodium-Centred Perspective</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4994</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">5005</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201501655</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D25%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D4994-5005%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26author%3DN.%2BSharma%26author%3DE.%2BGonzalo%26author%3DJ.%2BC.%2BPramudita%26author%3DM.%2BH.%2BHan%26author%3DH.%2BE.%2BA.%2BBrand%26author%3DJ.%2BN.%2BHart%26author%3DW.%2BK.%2BPang%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26author%3DT.%2BRojo%26title%3DThe%2BUnique%2BStructural%2BEvolution%2Bof%2Bthe%2BO3-Phase%2BNa2%252F3Fe2%252F3Mn1%252F3O2%2Bduring%2BHigh%2BRate%2BCharge%252FDischarge%253A%2BA%2BSodium-Centred%2BPerspective%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.201501655&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c17554&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.201501655&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Unique Structural Evolution of the O3-Phase Na2/3Fe2/3Mn1/3O2 during High Rate Charge/Discharge: A Sodium-Centred Perspective</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sharma, Neeraj; Gonzalo, Elena; Pramudita, James C.; Han, Man Huon; Brand, Helen E. A.; Hart, Judy N.; Pang, Wei Kong; Guo, Zaiping; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">31</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4994-5005</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of new insertion electrodes in sodium-ion batteries requires an in-depth understanding of the relationship between electrochem. performance and the structural evolution during cycling.  To date in situ synchrotron X-ray and neutron diffraction methods appear to be the only probes of in situ electrode evolution at high rates, a crit. condition for battery development.  Here, the structural evolution of the recently synthesized O3-phase of Na2/3Fe2/3Mn1/3O2 is reported under relatively high current rates.  The evolution of the phases, their lattice parameters, and phase fractions, and the sodium content in the crystal structure as a function of the charge/discharge process are shown.  It is found that the O3-phase persists throughout the charge/discharge cycle but undergoes a series of two-phase and solid-soln. transitions subtly modifying the sodium content and at. positions but keeping the overall space-group symmetry (structural motif).  In addn., for the first time, evidence of a structurally characterized region is shown that undergoes two-phase and solid-soln. phase transitions simultaneously.  The Mn/Fe-O bond lengths, c lattice parameter evolution, and the distance between the Mn/FeO6 layers are shown to concertedly change in a favorable manner for Na+ insertion/extn.  The exceptional electrochem. performance of this electrode can be related in part to the electrode maintaining the O3-phase throughout the charge/discharge process.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrSbB_8hmyREbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh47t0mqhO7iA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtFWns7jM&amp;md5=c001fd357f1e98b1b5f6566ed1e8c1da</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da889b2c7fb325-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

                        rightTab-cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phase Compatible NiFe2O4 Coating Tunes Oxygen Redox in Li-Rich Layered Oxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Jiming; Li, Yu; Chen, Zhiqiang; Liang, Gemeng; Hu, Sijiang; Zhou, Tengfei; Zheng, Fenghua; Pan, Qichang; Wang, Hongqiang; Li, Qingyu; Liu, Jianwen; Guo, Zaiping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-rich layered oxides have attracted intense attention for lithium-ion batteries, as provide substantial capacity from transition metal cation redox simultaneous with reversible oxygen-anion redox.  However, unregulated irreversible oxygen-anion redox leads to crit. issues such as voltage fade and oxygen release.  Here, we report a feasible NiFe2O4 (NFO) surface-coating strategy to turn the nonbonding coordination of surface oxygen into metal-oxygen decoordination.  In particular, the surface simplex M-O (M = Ni, Co, Mn from MO6 octahedra) and N-O (N = Ni, Fe from NO6 octahedra) bonds are reconstructed in the form of M-O-N bonds.  By applying both in operando and ex situ technologies, we found this heterostructural interface traps surface lattice oxygen, as well as restrains cation migration in Li-rich layered oxide during electrochem. cycling.  Therefore, surface lattice oxygen behavior is significantly sustained.  More interestingly, we directly observe the surface oxygen redox decouple with cation migration.  In addn., the NFO-coating blocks HF produced from electrolyte decompn., resulting in reducing the dissoln. of Mn.  With this strategy, higher cycle stability (91.8% at 1 C after 200 cycles) and higher rate capability (109.4 mA g-1 at 1 C) were achieved in this work, compared with pristine Li-rich layered oxide.  Our work offers potential for designing electrode materials utilizing oxygen redox chem.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpEDW4_1UaUpLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgabDhSa-qRaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhtlOhsrzL&amp;md5=60d7f0e1d8752c2168c65885e3dbe44d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1039/c6cs00776g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Myung, S.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-Ion Batteries: Present and Future</span>. <i>Chem. Soc. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>46</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3529</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3614</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c6cs00776g</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGot-2IKXj-Q-7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgabDhSa-qRaQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvF2rsbk%253D&amp;md5=cfc7b2d153696dcbded22d954ff06174</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2017.01.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Titirici, M.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances of Electrode Materials for Low-Cost Sodium-Ion Batteries towards Practical Application for Grid Energy Storage</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">130</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">151</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
